  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ecfceb5b-74b5-4513-ac1d-5386fd06e6db'
      });

  <span id="freeText13789034163140606520" style="display:none">The story that began with <i>Unwind</i> continues.<br /><br />Connor and Lev are on the run after the destruction of the Graveyard, the last safe haven for AWOL Unwinds. But for the first time, they’re not just running away from something. This time, they’re running toward answers, in the form of a woman Proactive Citizenry has tried to erase from history itself. If they can find her, and learn why the shadowy figures behind unwinding are so afraid of her, they may discover the key to bringing down unwinding forever.<br /><br />Cam, the rewound boy, is plotting to take down the organization that created him. Because he knows that if he can bring Proactive Citizenry to its knees, it will show Risa how he truly feels about her. And without Risa, Cam is having trouble remembering what it feels like to be human.<br /><br />With the Juvenile Authority and vindictive parts pirates hunting them, the paths of Connor, Lev, Cam, and Risa will converge explosively—and everyone will be changed.<br /><br />Neal Shusterman continues the adventure that VOYA called “poignant, compelling, and ultimately terrifying.”</span>

  <span id="freeText3756315572009851321" style="display:none">I was the lucky one who discovered Unwind only this year and had to wait just a bit to read Unwholly.<br>You poor people who had to wait 5 years! <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393487i/757591.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Well let's hope Unsouled will really be published in 2013 and preferably on January 1. right? <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380393487ra/757592.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> ;)<br><br>Update January 29 2016. <div id="review_635306389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/635306389" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/635306389?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=super-sidekicks">super-sidekicks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer635306389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15251005855327587480">Reread/buddy read with some fellow BBBers<br/><br/>While this is my least favorite book of the series it is still a strong 4 star read for me. I love the character development and the way even more of the history of unwinding is shown to the reader. The first read through I was a little distracted waiting for Conner and Risa to find each other again, but this read through I could sit back and really take in the story. So many heart wrenching moments, Cam and Una especially torn at my heartstrings. Even be</span>
  <span id="freeText15251005855327587480" style="display:none">Reread/buddy read with some fellow BBBers<br /><br />While this is my least favorite book of the series it is still a strong 4 star read for me. I love the character development and the way even more of the history of unwinding is shown to the reader. The first read through I was a little distracted waiting for Conner and Risa to find each other again, but this read through I could sit back and really take in the story. So many heart wrenching moments, Cam and Una especially torn at my heartstrings. Even better the second time through. <br /><br />4 Strong Stars<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“You want to know the real reason unwinding keeps going strong, Miss Risa Ward? It’s because of the things we’re willing to do to save our children.” She thinks about it and laughs ruefully. “Imagine that. We’re willing to sacrifice the children we don’t love for the ones we do…”</i>
</b><br /><br />Neal Shusterman is a genius story teller. He builds his stories layer by layer, revealing the plot through multiple POVs. While the majority of POVs are from Connor, Lev, Risa and Cam the others all add so much to the depth and thought put into all aspects of the book. It is like a chess board and he is moving all the pieces of the puzzle around letting you see most of the plays before the final conclusion of the game. Some pieces will be sacrificed, some will only be distractions, some support and others will sneak in change the game completely. But inevitably the game will end with a victor, who that victor will be and how s still anyone’s guess.<br /><br />I’m wowed by this story. The initial horror that I felt in Unwind by the atrocities committed in that book haven’t left me and even when I think I can’t be more horrified by anything else in this series I’m proven wrong again. From who is really controlling the clappers to what Proactive Citizenry is willing to do or has done to keep all the body parts coming.<br /><br />Neal Shusterman lets us walk through unwinding’s past as the scientist Jansen Rheinschild horrified by what he has invented and how it is to be used tries to correct his mistakes. At the beginning of each Part there is a snippet of Jansen’s past leading to a better understanding of the present. Neal is also great at showing what is going on in the present story with some of the propaganda and commercial ads that are being ran. This is a brilliant mechanism in the story as it lets the reader see what society is really like.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Connor and Lev</b>
</u> - Are on the run together trying to get to Sonia who might have a key to why Proactive Citizenry would have erased her husband from history. They hope it is a key on how to stop unwinding all together. But along the way they run into a few obstacles and end up meeting Grace as well as a few friends from Lev’s past. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>No true hero ever believes that they are one,” she tells him. “So you go ahead, Lev, and keep denying it with every fiber of you being.”</i>
</b><br /><br />It’s clear the Lev still has a major part to play in the downfall of the system. He just isn’t sure what it is yet.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Cam</b>
</u> - Cam is struggling with who and what he is, does he even have a soul is he more than just a collection of all of his parts. Cam is determined to make the people who rewound him pay. He still believes that will make Risa love him and that is the only thing he wants.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Cam knows beyond a shadow of a doubt he could fill that void in her, if only she loved him enough to let him. It would be the one thing that would make him feel whole. </i>
</b><br /><br />Cam is putting all his trust into loving Risa. But he still doesn’t know that Connor is alive and maybe there isn’t any room in Risa’s heart to love him that way. He is definitely a wild card because what will he do if he doesn’t get the girl he wants.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Risa</b>
</u> - Risa knows the ADR is in shambles but she wants to help revive it. Although she misses Connor, I like that she is never so consumed by it that she drops all of her goals to help the Unwinds to just look for him. Risa stays on her own path and while she hopes to see him again she sticks to the bigger picture of trying to find a way to fight against the system. She even runs into an old friend of Lev’s along the way CyFy. I was so happy to see that kid again. He still has a very interesting story and it is interesting to see how some people with unwound parts choose to live.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Starkey</b>
</u> - Is evil and awful and a complete freaking psychopath. But he is a charismatic psychopath who is leading a band of stork kids escaped from the Graveyard. Every time I think Starkey can’t do anything more horrendous well he does and I become even more disgusted with him. He is the ultimate bad guy, looking only for glory and immortality willing to sacrifice anyone and everyone else to get it. I love hating him.<br /><br />There are some other characters that really add to the story. Grace is a new addition to the AWOLs as she is traveling with Conner. I really liked the way she is simple minded yet an idiot savant at strategy and is a great addition to the team. We get to see Hayden again I was worried about what happened to him after he was captured in Unwholly. <br /><br />There was a lot of development of the individual characters in this book. Cam and Starkey especially I see as more three dimensional now. Conner, Risa and Lev have changed so much from when they first escaped together. My one and only complaint is I really wanted Conner and Risa to find each other sooner, but I can’t even be mad about that because it was perfect how it happened.<br /><br />The big reveal at the end was a little shocking but not unexpected and I really believe that this book was the best jumping board it could be going into the final book of the series. It was emotionally gripping and I stayed locked into the story the entire time waiting to see what would come next. Neal Shusterman has his work cut out for him to make the final book as strong as the rest of the series but he has a great lead in with this book and I can’t help but feel that everything in the last book will be absolutely epic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15251005855327587480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399297869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10646234134101316286">Though my least favourite of the series but still a fantastic read. Absolutely fantastic. <br/><br/>This series has easily become one of my favourites and as eager as I am to see how it all concludes, I’m also incredibly sand to see it end. <br/><br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_642154428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/642154428" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/642154428?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer642154428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1173780744185493454">Do you ever just stare at people and think "wow, I really want to caress your brain?" Or, in more normal phrasing, have you ever admired someone's intelligence from afar? I've felt that way with several of my professors this semester, but I would love to just sit in a room with Neal Shusterman's brain (or Neal Shusterman himself, I suppose) and ask: how do you do it? How do you write? How do you breathe the same air us humans do?<br/><br/>On a more serious note, <i>UnSouled</i> serves as the third book of the Un</span>
  <span id="freeText1173780744185493454" style="display:none">Do you ever just stare at people and think "wow, I really want to caress your brain?" Or, in more normal phrasing, have you ever admired someone's intelligence from afar? I've felt that way with several of my professors this semester, but I would love to just sit in a room with Neal Shusterman's brain (or Neal Shusterman himself, I suppose) and ask: how do you do it? How do you write? How do you breathe the same air us humans do?<br /><br />On a more serious note, <i>UnSouled</i> serves as the third book of the Unwind Dystology (sorry for the abundance of parentheticals, but is that a real world? Anyone?) Authorities still arrest teens and unwind them for their organs and body parts, but Shusterman raises the stakes as new laws concerning the unwinding of adults and a repeal of Cap-17 garner political attention. The book follows Connor, Lev, Cam, and Risa, but voices from the second book like Starkey and new characters like Grace get time in the spotlight too. Three sides of an inevitable war arise: those in favor of unwinding, those who will use violence to avenge the unwound, and those who wish to end it for good.<br /><br />As always, Shusterman balances a wealth of points of view, an intense and layered plot, and a host of societal issues. While some YA authors who write dystopia tend to favor one aspect of the story, like the romance, the world-building, etc. Shusterman develops it all with finesse. He draws from old conflicts, like Connor's relationship with his parents, in addition to new ones, like the competition between Cam and Connor. In the end we're left to think for ourselves - what makes people people? How significant is each individual part of us in comparison to the whole? What really comprises that whole aside from our organs and bones?<br /><br />While <i>UnSouled</i> felt like the typical middle installment that plodded along for the sake of preparation, Shusterman's talent kept me invested. I eagerly anticipate the emotional bomb that will be <i>Undivided</i> and I highly recommend this series to all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1173780744185493454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1399683218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399683218" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399683218?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terence" href="/user/show/23206148-terence">Terence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442423695" href="/book/show/17334446-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399683218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6053917542038277539">After the destruction of the graveyard Connor and Lev are once again running, but this time they aren't just running away from something. They are running to find answers. Connor believes the answers will come from an old friend who he's discovered is so much more than she appeared.<br/><br/>Make no mistake UnSouled is a transition book. Most large series have at least one and UnSouled is the transition book for the Unwind Dystology. The board is being set, the pieces are taking their places, and events a</span>
  <span id="freeText6053917542038277539" style="display:none">After the destruction of the graveyard Connor and Lev are once again running, but this time they aren't just running away from something. They are running to find answers. Connor believes the answers will come from an old friend who he's discovered is so much more than she appeared.<br /><br />Make no mistake UnSouled is a transition book. Most large series have at least one and UnSouled is the transition book for the Unwind Dystology. The board is being set, the pieces are taking their places, and events are about to become explosive...in the next book. This book is a bit slower with more parts that didn't feel quite as important as the events in the previous two books in the series, but there is still a lot of great storytelling happening here.<br /><br />First off I have to discuss the curious case of Camus Comprix because his existence at this point makes no sense. I assumed at some point the purpose of his creation would be made clear, but after two books it seems Neal Shusterman and Proactive Citizenry made him for the same reason...just because they could. On top of that his own motives are inexplicable. Cam basically fell for a picture of a girl who he came to learn thought he was a monster and by the end of book two had some respect for him. So what does Cam do because of this? Vows to take down his makers who have provided him with a lavish lifestyle to say it nicely. He has minimal reasoning for practically all his behaviors and he's kind of <i>harshing my vibe</i> when I'm reading the book. I get it he had no choice in being made, but I can't feel sympathetic for him.<br /><br />I love Grace. I love that nothing about her is standard. She isn't a beautiful girl to be saved or gawked at. Grace is described as "not fat, but heavyset and unshapely. Dowdy..." Also that "[t]he slack expression on her face speaks of a dullness that isn't her fault." She's immediately introduced as being a low cortical which I imagine is supposed to say she has a mental disorder of some sort. Don't be blinded by her outward appearance or slack face because she is something special and the story displays it quickly and often. I just loved her.<br /><br />I'd be remiss to not mention Starkey. When he first arrived in the story I thought he was a murdering version of Roland, but this young man is far more capable and resourceful than I could have ever imagine. He builds on his ruthlessness and resourcefulness from UnWholly. If the AWOL unwinds simply needed to go to war to stop unwinding then Starkey is undoubtedly one of it's best options for a general.<br /><br />UnSouled was a good story and I'm excited to see what happens next in the dark world of the Unwind Dystology.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6053917542038277539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9009708055961825859">Lots going on in this third installment of the Unwind dystology! This book is definitely a part of a series (you can't read it out of order). Also there are too many things that are left unresolved at the end and lots of POV characters so not a ton of advancement in plot for each person - you get bits and pieces (no pun intended) and then the POV switches to someone else.   <span id="freeText9009708055961825859" style="display:none">Lots going on in this third installment of the Unwind dystology! This book is definitely a part of a series (you can't read it out of order). Also there are too many things that are left unresolved at the end and lots of POV characters so not a ton of advancement in plot for each person - you get bits and pieces (no pun intended) and then the POV switches to someone else. I really don't like spending too much time in Nelson or Starkey's heads and would have rather stayed with Conner, Risa and Lev. Many times I had to flip back to the earlier sections to remind myself what's was going on with a certain character. I'm going to take a break but will return to this world soon as I need to finish it up!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_495168415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/495168415" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/495168415?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442423695" href="/book/show/17334446-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer495168415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18398754687511449830">After a SUPER long time, I finally got around to reading this. <i>Unwind</i> is one of my favorite books; it totally blew me away the first time I read it. And the sequel, <i>UnWholly</i>, did an excellent job of complicating the plot and bringing in some intriguing new characters. I recently re-read books 1 and 2 (in preparation for finally reading books 3 and 4), and they were just as brilliant the second time around.<br/><br/>I have to say, <i>UnSouled</i> is not my favorite of the series so far. Don't get me wrong––I stil</span>
  <span id="freeText18398754687511449830" style="display:none">After a SUPER long time, I finally got around to reading this. <i>Unwind</i> is one of my favorite books; it totally blew me away the first time I read it. And the sequel, <i>UnWholly</i>, did an excellent job of complicating the plot and bringing in some intriguing new characters. I recently re-read books 1 and 2 (in preparation for finally reading books 3 and 4), and they were just as brilliant the second time around.<br><br>I have to say, <i>UnSouled</i> is not my favorite of the series so far. Don't get me wrong––I still liked it. I enjoyed seeing more of the world and characters Shusterman has created. Like <i>UnWholly</i>, it continues to build upon the complex world and conflict. <br><br>But while I felt like <i>UnWholly</i> stood well on its own, I feel like <i>UnSouled</i> ... didn't. It was good, but I felt like it wandered more and didn't have as much of a concrete plot as the first two books did. I've been told by a few people that it's the weakest of the series, and that more than anything it's kind of a "stepping stone" between books 2 and 4. And I definitely got that sense from it––like it was just a small piece of a bigger whole (for lack of a better phrase, haha ... ha). <br><br>That said, it's still an enjoyable book and an interesting addition to the series. Like the first two books, it continues to explore a lot of complex ethical and political themes. As always, I'm awed by Neal Shusterman's world-building, characterization, and attention to detail. He obviously puts a lot of thought into his stories and the worlds in which they take place. <br><br>There weren't a lot of new characters in this one, but I was kind of grateful for that. While <i>UnWholly</i> threw in lots of new characters left and right, I appreciated that <i>UnSouled</i> focused more on fleshing out the characters we already know. (Side note: I was pretty disappointed Miracolina wasn't in this book at all, because she was one of my favorite characters from the second book. But hopefully she'll show up again in book 4??)<br><br>Anyway: over all I liked this one, even if it wasn't the best of the series. And I'm really looking forward to reading the last book! <br><br><b>Pre-release fangirling under the cut.</b><br><br>----------<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br><b>2013:</b><br><br>Official release date: October 15th. YES. This means I don't have to wait another five years!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403497ra/785024.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh and it has a cover now!<br>*Looks at cover*<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403497ra/785025.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>HOLY SHIT THAT COVER IS TERRIFYING AS BALLS. <br><br>I love it.<br><br><b>Update</b>: Oh ... now it's not coming out until November. *Pouts* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_331884823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331884823" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331884823?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442423695" href="/book/show/17334446-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331884823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9021739131196211152"> <a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/08/unsouled-by-neal-shusterman.html' rel='nofollow noopener'> Check out Scott Reads It! for reviews, giveaways, & more!</a> <br/>Unwind and Unwholly are two of my favorite books of all time and Neal Shusterman never ceases to amaze me with each book I read by him. Though Unwind was originally slated to be a trilogy, Unsouled wound up being too voluminous to be one book. S&S split Unwind's conclusion into Unsouled and Undivided and the Unwind Trilogy became a "Dystology". <br/><br/>Unsouled is definitely a worthy sequel to Unwholly, it delivers a thrilling story that is dis</span>
  <span id="freeText9021739131196211152" style="display:none"> <a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/08/unsouled-by-neal-shusterman.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> Check out Scott Reads It! for reviews, giveaways, &amp; more!</a> <br />Unwind and Unwholly are two of my favorite books of all time and Neal Shusterman never ceases to amaze me with each book I read by him. Though Unwind was originally slated to be a trilogy, Unsouled wound up being too voluminous to be one book. S&amp;S split Unwind's conclusion into Unsouled and Undivided and the Unwind Trilogy became a "Dystology". <br /><br />Unsouled is definitely a worthy sequel to Unwholly, it delivers a thrilling story that is disturbing and absolutely engrossing. The story is a bit slower paced than the previous novels and this is definitely the most character driven of all of the Unwind books. Throughout the novel, readers will enthralled by the perfectly written dialogue and action scenes. Shusterman manages to alternate from the 3rd person point-of-view of more characters than ever; this also means that there are more converging storylines than before. Despite the numerous point-of-views and storylines, everything is neatly done and it never feels overwhelming. A lot of books lose a sense of poignancy when they are written in 3rd person, but Shusterman fills his writing with so much emotion and power.<br /><br />In Unsouled, I lost so much respect for Lev and Connor, two characters who I used to love immensely. My perception of them dived during Unsouled and it's a bit disconcerting. Nevertheless Shusterman still manages to make his characters breathe and 3 dimensional, each in their own way. Though I'm no longer huge fans of Lev or Connor, it is extremely impressive how Shusterman juggles so many characters and manages to make each character completely distinct. <br /><br />The story ARC in Unsouled never seems to fully take off and it seems to be stuck in one spot. Though I loved Unsouled, it feels as if something is missing because Unsouled is really apart of a larger picture. In order to have fully appreciated Unsouled, I feel like I needed to have read Undivided so I fully understood the grand schematics of the finale to Unwind. I personally believe Unsouled and Undivided would probably have worked better as one large novel so readers don't feel as if they're missing out on the complete story. Unsouled didn't work too well on it's own and I feel bad judging it based on that aspect. <br /><br />Unsouled is a great novel, it's just a not-so great 1/2 of a conclusion to the Unwind Dystology. I loved where the story was going, it just ended way too soon and right when I was most engaged. I personally would recommend reading Unsouled and Undivided back-to-back instead of reading them separately. I wish I had waited to read Unsouled so I wouldn't have to wait so long to read a continuation of a story that I hold so dear to me. Unsouled is everything one would expect from Neal Shusterman and a sequel to Unwholly, it's just feels unfair to have an "unwound" book -- a book that is only bits and pieces of a larger body. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9021739131196211152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12743651535452311391" style="display:none">This is what might have happened if the plight of teens was turned into an industry of Frankenstein's monsters. <br /><br />You know, the older folks shamelessly profiting on the consumption of young flesh.<br /><br />No, no, this is NOT an accurate reflection of our modern society! No, no, not at all.<br /><br />Ahem.<br /><br />Well! I honestly hoped that the first book would continue on into a MUCH darker and nastier dystopia. Instead, we just get the normal kind of social dystopia that villainizes an underclass in order to perpetuate the massive profitization. <br /><br />No, no, this is obviously NOT an accurate reflection of our modern society! No, no, not at all.<br /><br />Even if it doesn't go in the direction I had hoped, it's still a pretty good skewer. You could almost cut and paste the whole non-SF setup and apply it to so many modern protest groups and see a pretty obvious correlation. <br /><br />Key points: don't get violent, focus on peaceful protest, but don't forget... they will lie. It's an unenviable position. Let's hope you don't lose all your body parts, too.</span>

  <span id="freeText5163901204612431546" style="display:none">I re-read the first 2 books. <br>I read this one.<br>My mind is a mess.<br>I loved it! (ALL)<br><br><b>Full Review:</b><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-unsouled.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415204603i/11750874.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It’s official, this is <s>one of</s> the best dystopian stories I’ve ever had the honour to read!<br><br>To be <i>this</i> connected with the characters, this emotionally invested in the story, this awestruck with the world building and the amazing, mind-blowing plot.. It feels like a gift, there’s no better feeling in the reading world.<br><br>Looking back to where it started, making an inventory of all the characters that came along since there, and watching their paths converge time and time again… I tell you, this story is an actual masterpiece.<br><br>My mind is a bit fuzzy, I’ve been on an Unwind marathon and it’s hard to pinpoint (exactly) all the qualities this particular book has inside the series. It starts with all hell breaking loose in the graveyard and it takes all characters on this awesome adventure around the US.<br><br>All puzzle pieces start to fall into place, unlikely alliances are made, people tag along for this journey in order to find a way to freedom, while others make their own goals and plan to reach them, sooner rather than later.<br><br>Our trio gets together and apart more than not (in one format or another), the reunions are bittersweet and unexpected. More villains start to track their movements and I can’t describe my excitement towards the next book in the series, as this one left me breathless and begging for more.<br><br>I’ve said this again and again, I’ll do it once more: what makes this story this amazingly great is the plausibility of it all. Yes, there are many fortunate and unfortunate coincidences, I’ll give it that - though I think that this is part of its charm, but the overall story, the world itself (so complex and mind-blowing) is painfully realistically portrayed.<br><br><b>This series is breathtaking.<br>It is mind-blowing.<br>It sweeps you out off your feet.<br>It puts things into perspective.<br>It gives you a sense of what humanity is, and what the lack of it can mean for the human kind.<br>It is gruesome and awesome and I can never have enough of it.</b><br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/neal-shusterman/review-unsouled.html" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_578478790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/578478790" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14461220-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458426069p2/14461220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578478790?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/14461220-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578478790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2333080224535603699"><u>AFTER</u> <br/><br/>Can I say wow?! Haunting, chilling, Neal Shusterman has done it again in this astonishing series that pushes the boundaries and explores some very possible feasibilities in our society today. <br/><br/>We continue on with the tale of Connor and Lev and the reader watches glued in fascination and horror as we see their paths coincide with the paths of Lisa and Cam and a few other amazing friends and terrifying enemies in between. <br/><br/>What I love so much about this series is the world-building. Neal Shust</span>
  <span id="freeText2333080224535603699" style="display:none"><u>AFTER</u> <br><br>Can I say wow?! Haunting, chilling, Neal Shusterman has done it again in this astonishing series that pushes the boundaries and explores some very possible feasibilities in our society today. <br><br>We continue on with the tale of Connor and Lev and the reader watches glued in fascination and horror as we see their paths coincide with the paths of Lisa and Cam and a few other amazing friends and terrifying enemies in between. <br><br>What I love so much about this series is the world-building. Neal Shusterman sucks the reader into what scarily seems like a very possible world. It's kind of like that moment when you read the book 1984 and you see elements of the totalitarian government today. In Unsouled, the book continues to explore the very frightening and unique concept of unwinding, the "compromise" between pro-lifers and pro-choice people in the abortion battle. The compromise? No abortions are allowed, but parents may choose to "unwind" their children during the ages of 12-17* (according to a law passed in the previous book), where children are literally divided up into body parts and organs which are then used in surgeries to provide body parts to other people. The book calls it "living in a divided state." <br><br>But what is even more gripping and haunting about this series is that in between each chapter or part, the author presents real-life examples that he used to extrapolate this unbelievable reality. Let me provide you with some examples...<br><br>1. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.naturalnews.com/036052_organ_harvesting_kidneys_black_market.html">http://www.naturalnews.com/036052_org...</a> - Article titled "Global Organ Harvesting a Booming Black Market Business; A Kidney Harvested Every Hour"<br>2. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/10/08/charlie-fuqua-arkansas-candidate-death-penalty-rebellious-children_n_1948490.html">http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/10...</a> - Article titled "Charlie Fuqua, Arkansas Legislative Candidate, Endorses Death Penalty For Rebellious Children In Book"<br><br>Now before you dismiss this as bogus, radical, and unrealistic, I urge you to read this amazing series. <br><br>And not only does it question the quintessential question of what life is, the book also also has an action-packed plot, characters you simply fall in love with and learn to hate, and it prevents you from putting it down. I recommend this book series to absolutely everyone and that if you haven't read this, GO READ IT NOW. <br><br>That is all. Now excuse me while I go deal with my feels. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389001716ra/7968747.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>BEFORE</u><br><u>EDIT: April 9</u><br><br>What a creepy cover... *shivers* <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415914ra/821285.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415914ra/821286.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is all. <br><br><u>Earlier</u><br><br>October 15th??? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415914ra/821287.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/485361.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2333080224535603699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <i>4 of 5 stars<br/><br/>----- </i>

I loved how this series managed to consistently make the readers be thrilled about the next events. There is no boring moments.   <i>4 of 5 stars<br /><br />----- </i>
</b><br /><br />The different perspective converging into one plot is what makes this book so special. I loved how this series managed to consistently make the readers be thrilled about the next events. There is no boring moments. You can have your own theories of what was going to happen, but you can't settle on those theories because, even though this was not exactly jaw-dropping, this can still get you on the edge of your seat. This book was smart, with the right amount of tension. A very solid read. I was seriously getting anxious from time to time as if I was just another fugitive running with these fugitive characters. I am so very excited, with a hint of sadness at the same time, to pick up the last book. I know I'm going to love the conclusion as much, if not more, as the first three books.</span>

  <span id="freeText13655311666683842346" style="display:none">4.5 stars and I believe the series is improving book-to-book. I think another reviewer may have summarized it best: "Neal Shusterman weaves a tale as interesting and complex as Camus Comprix's 'internal community.'" The story continues to develop layer by layer, with multiple POV, primarily Connor, Lev, Risa and Cam. Weaved into this story is the backstory of unwinding's inventor, scientist Jansen Rheinschild and his wife, Sonia, who we've seen before. Connor and Lev are on the lam together, trying to reach Sonia, whom they believe can help them stop unwindings. Along the way, they pick up a fascinating new character, Grace, who is simple of mind, but very attuned to emotions and plays an important role in the book. Really looking forward to the conclusion.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9298809507754899637">Another awesome installment in the UNWIND series. Our cast of characters continues to be stirred around like cherrios in a bowl of milk, going from place to place, meeting up, then being separated, finding friends and foes, Neal Shusterman has created a super exciting world and this was a great building of tension. <br/><br/>I particularly liked the inclusion of the <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ reservations that were now safe havens within the US because they did not support unwinding and finding out more about what h</span></span>
  <span id="freeText9298809507754899637" style="display:none">Another awesome installment in the UNWIND series. Our cast of characters continues to be stirred around like cherrios in a bowl of milk, going from place to place, meeting up, then being separated, finding friends and foes, Neal Shusterman has created a super exciting world and this was a great building of tension. <br /><br />I particularly liked the inclusion of the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ reservations that were now safe havens within the US because they did not support unwinding and finding out more about what happened to Lev before he became a clapper. And I especially liked seeing Cam strike up with our regular gang of Connor and Lev (and Risa!) even if only for a bit. Cam is a character it's hard not to feel sympathy for. The idea of him is monstrous, an abomination, but it was never his idea to be made, as he points out. The abomination is really someone else's (his creator's) mind, not his, not him. He and Una make a funny/scary but potentially cute couple.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Excited to read the final book! 4.5/5 stars.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/746500909" />
    <a title="Meaghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13867757-meaghan"><img alt="Meaghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364092248p2/13867757.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13867757-meaghan?shelf=2013-books">2013-books</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13867757-meaghan?shelf=post-apocolytic-dystopian">post-apocolytic-dystopian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer746500909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14055178825135625552">This series is holding strong! I loved this third installment of the Unwind dystology (whatever a dystology is). If a dystology is this amazing, I think more authors should consider them though!<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383061584i/6367395.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have no clue how Mr. Shusterman makes me care for so many characters. There are so many POV switches and so many characters, that I feel under normal circumstances I would not care about any of them. However, this is not a normal circumstance and I have some kind of emotional attachment (whether that be</span>
  <span id="freeText14055178825135625552" style="display:none">This series is holding strong! I loved this third installment of the Unwind dystology (whatever a dystology is). If a dystology is this amazing, I think more authors should consider them though!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1383061584i/6367395.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have no clue how Mr. Shusterman makes me care for so many characters. There are so many POV switches and so many characters, that I feel under normal circumstances I would not care about any of them. However, this is not a normal circumstance and I have some kind of emotional attachment (whether that be love or hate or somewhere in between) for all of them. Each character is also very distinct from each other in their POV. I don't know how Neal does it!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382997253ra/6326064.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another thing I love about this book (as scary as it is), is that Mr. Shusterman makes the world believable. Especially when he adds real articles from our society and he puts so many parallels from our lives into the book. From just a brief synopsis, this concept sounds utterly horrifying and unrealistic but the world created becomes more and more believable the further in you read.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382997253ra/6326065.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really like the addition of Grace's character. She is a really interesting character and her POV is fascinating. This is about how I feel listening to Grace come up with her strategies.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382997253ra/6326066.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Connor, Risa, and Lev are all back in this story (obviously) and I still love them all! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And yay for Connor and Risa finding each other again!!! I'm not quite sure where they stand romantically but yay!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I am also happy to see Lev growing as a character. He seems to be the character that grows the most for me from book to book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am excited to see how he goes after the parts pirates and what he has planned for after he catches them.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There are also plenty of bad guys lurking around in this book. Starkey, Argent, Nelson, juvenile authority, etc. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Maybe Cam?! Still don't know what to think of him.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's crazy how much is going on in these stories and I still know exactly what is happening and it hasn't all become convoluted. As for Starkey...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ something more is going to have to come out of him becoming a dad...crazy!! That's the last person that should have children...  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382997253ra/6326067.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then there is Bam and Hayden...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Not quite sure what is going to happen here but it's an interesting dynamic.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Cam is kind of the outlier here. I have no idea what to think of him at this point (which I'm sure is what the author wants). <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I wonder if he'll tell them about Connor and Risa thinking he can let Connor get unwound, or whatever may happen to him, while he protects Risa. I hope not but it's a strong possibility in my mind. He seems to act emotionally when it comes to Risa.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The end of this book was great!! I was wondering what was going to happen and did not see this coming. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I really hope the science doesn't become completely botched! This is an interesting parallel with things like 3D printers that are being made right now. And this is not a completely crazy idea. This type of science is actually being considered. Here is some information on it if anyone wants to nerd out as much as me on it...<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.livescience.com/39885-3d-printing-to-deliver-organs.html">http://www.livescience.com/39885-3d-p...</a> <br><br>In addition, it's also not a crazy concept that a big industry would shut down or deny a better technology/scientific advancement because of the money being made on the current technology. I won't go into my rant on this one but this does happen quite a bit.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I can't wait for the next book!!!! It has every component to be a completely epic finale!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382997253ra/6326068.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14055178825135625552" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1100294277" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1100294277" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513342355p2/8409451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1100294277?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/8409451-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100294277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6510871298697760612">4.5<br/><br/>“Hope can be bruised and battered. It can be forced underground and even rendered unconscious, but hope cannot be killed.”<br/><br/><br/><b> The skinny: </b><br/><br/>Lev and Connor have one clue that is driving them forward: Janson Rheinschild. They believe that by seeking out the woman connected to Janson that they can find the answers to the end of unwinding. Unbeknownst to Connor and Lev, while they are trying to unravel the mystery of Rheinschild, Nelson is still on their trail. Nelson has not given up his goal to capt</span>
  <span id="freeText6510871298697760612" style="display:none">4.5<br /><br />“Hope can be bruised and battered. It can be forced underground and even rendered unconscious, but hope cannot be killed.”<br /><br /><br /><b> The skinny: </b><br /><br />Lev and Connor have one clue that is driving them forward: Janson Rheinschild. They believe that by seeking out the woman connected to Janson that they can find the answers to the end of unwinding. Unbeknownst to Connor and Lev, while they are trying to unravel the mystery of Rheinschild, Nelson is still on their trail. Nelson has not given up his goal to capture them, not in the slightest. Cam, inconsolable after Risa leaves, is taking out his anger and frustrations on the organization responsible for his ‘rewinding’. His plan, his obsession, is to take down Proactive Citizenry. Risa, on her own, is unsure of who she can trust. She desperately searches out a safe location to stay while she waits to be reunited with her friends. With the help of friends, the drive of determination, and the power of hope, these four characters meet again and learn answers that could change everything.<br /><br /><br /><b>The reivew:</b><br /><br />I liked Unwind. I liked UnWholly even a little bit more. But I pretty much loved UnSouled. <br /><br /><br />I made a little listy-poo to help me organize why I liked this book so much:<br /><br /><br />1) The first reason I liked this book was also present in previous stories, but I noticed it more so in this installment. I really appreciated that all of the kids/young adults in this book excel in one area or another. At first this annoyed me because I couldn’t understand how every character could be SO brilliant in one concentrated area or another (technology, leadership, etc.) – it just didn’t seem realistic. It was particularly hard to swallow the fact that even the characters that were supposed to be less intelligent were basically awesome masterminds. But then I started to look at it a little differently. I began to think that maybe, as an adult, I underestimate the intelligence and drive of young people. Perhaps the author wanted the readers to see each person in the novel as important and valuable in their own right. Possibly he wanted me (and I’m sure other adults) to not limit the capabilities of others. There is the real possibility that we don’t know what someone is really capable of until they are put into a situation where they have no other choice than to be amazing. MAYBE I’m seeing too much into this, but I just really ended up liking that aspect of the novel (in an I-hated-it-then-loved-it-because-I-over-think-things kinda way). <br /><br /><br />2) The second reason I liked this novel is the emphasis placed on the creation of unwinding. It was fascinating to see how Shusterman spun that aspect of the book. I really felt for the people who, inadvertently, invented the one thing that would change the history of the world as they knew it in such a disturbing way. It was saddening to see how people who just wanted to help the human population, instead see the horror that they caused.<br /><br /><br />3) The third reason was that the “Oooos and Ahhhhs” in this book really wowed me. There was one particular ‘reveal’ that I hadn’t anticipated. When this ‘reveal’ occurred, it really hit me hard; it not only made me feel like my insides were being squeezed, but also really made me think <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the part where it was realized that Cam had Wil’s hands  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It made me think about the process of unwinding, specifically unwinding that happens due to parts pirates. I thought deeply about what it must be like for someone to be caught, for someone to know they are going to die, and for family/friends to know that someone has been taken to be unwound. <br /><br /><br /><b>Overall</b>: <br /><br />These were only a few things that stuck out to me. Generally I enjoyed this book more than the previous two because I felt like the process of unwinding and the setting of the story had been established. I felt like this book allowed me to focus more on the emotional aspect, and less on the sensationalism of unwinding itself. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6510871298697760612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1695197680?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/22583265-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=why-would-ya">why-would-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=reads-with-buddies">reads-with-buddies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=dystopians">dystopians</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7091879-stepheny?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1695197680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5057581257962431736">Unsouled is the third book in the Unwind series. And probably the most forgettable.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484168279ra/21689616.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The characters I had grown to love in the first two books all come to a halting stop in this edition. The gang is all split up and everyone’s angry and confused. No one knows where they’re going or why they’re doing anything. They can’t make a decision about anything. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484168581ra/21689674.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It’s like all of a sudden our once-heroic MC’s just shut down completely. It’s probably the BIGGEST downfall of every YA series ever written. Katnis</span>
  <span id="freeText5057581257962431736" style="display:none">Unsouled is the third book in the Unwind series. And probably the most forgettable.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484168279ra/21689616.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The characters I had grown to love in the first two books all come to a halting stop in this edition. The gang is all split up and everyone’s angry and confused. No one knows where they’re going or why they’re doing anything. They can’t make a decision about anything. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484168581ra/21689674.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It’s like all of a sudden our once-heroic MC’s just shut down completely. It’s probably the BIGGEST downfall of every YA series ever written. Katniss shuts down in Mockingjay. Bella(grosssssssss) shuts down in pretty much every scenario in every single Twilight book. Tris and Four both have moments in the Divergent series where they shut down in some way. It’s fucking exhausting and stupid and YA writers need to STOP doing this. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484169955ra/21689821.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously. Fans do not want wishy-washy indecisive MC’s. We want kick-ass ones who go into every endeavor without thinking or planning. It’s exciting! It’s fun! It’s a fantastic reading experience! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484169873ra/21689813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I just really was let down after having read the first two books. They were so promising. But there were just way too many story lines going and I felt like the author lost his sense of direction somewhere along the way. Or was trying to make too many statements at once. It just left me feeling very unexcited about reading the final installment.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465598723ra/19378313.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1951931939" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1951931939" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11913659-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450473254p2/11913659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1951931939?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/11913659-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19432805-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=read-in-print">read-in-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=worth-a-re-read">worth-a-re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=social-messages">social-messages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11913659-jen?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1951931939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12230880185669539387">While this book had a couple of problems for me, I'm still giving it the 5 end of 4+ stars. <br/><br/>There is a bit of a stall midway, but even there Shusterman keeps things somewhat lively. And just about the time I thought he was going to descend into "I'm going to decide what's best for someone else no matter how they feel about it" territory, he saved things. I can't stand that plot device because it is so disrespectful of the person about whom things are being decided - all in the name of love, usua</span>
  <span id="freeText12230880185669539387" style="display:none">While this book had a couple of problems for me, I'm still giving it the 5 end of 4+ stars. <br /><br />There is a bit of a stall midway, but even there Shusterman keeps things somewhat lively. And just about the time I thought he was going to descend into "I'm going to decide what's best for someone else no matter how they feel about it" territory, he saved things. I can't stand that plot device because it is so disrespectful of the person about whom things are being decided - all in the name of love, usually. <br /><br />The series is starting to become about teenagers single-handedly saving the world. But there are still no special snowflakes and the themes in the story far outweigh any dislikable plot elements. I was surprised at the ending, but quite honestly it gave me hope. Shusterman has opted to include current-day articles throughout. I didn't realise they were actual links to actual articles until I tried one out of curiousity. I thought they were fictional and thrown in for effect. Reading these adds to the creepy sense that this plot could actually happen.<br /><br />I'll be interested to see how this series concludes. And while I am sure the novellas available will be heart-wrenching, they will also be hopeful. This story is indeed a cautionary tale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12230880185669539387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
