  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_797079597" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/797079597" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797079597?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the series who also enjoyed Unstrung</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=on-going-series">on-going-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=speculative-fiction">speculative-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve">bermuda-triangle-of-lurrrve</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=stereotypes">stereotypes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=roadtrip">roadtrip</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797079597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer742684348553882073"><i>
  <b><u>SPOILERS FOR UNWIND &UNWHOLLY AND A FEW PLOT POINTS HERE BUT NOTHING MAJOR</u><br/><br/>2.5 STARS<br/><blockquote>"Sometimes Lev, I just want to smack you."</blockquote></b>
</i><br/>But I'm getting way ahead of myself there. It's probably the disorientation talking because I'm still reeling from the <b>WHAT THE HELL HAPPENED???</b> pinging inside my brain. This review will probably echo a lot of 2-star sentiments but I ended up giving it a hopeful 3 because something about Connor still reminds me a little of Jack Bauer.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388766328ra/7924384.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <br/>The biggest chunk of the story con</span>
  <span id="freeText742684348553882073" style="display:none"><i>
  <b><u>SPOILERS FOR UNWIND &amp;UNWHOLLY AND A FEW PLOT POINTS HERE BUT NOTHING MAJOR</u><br><br>2.5 STARS<br><blockquote>"Sometimes Lev, I just want to smack you."</blockquote></b>
</i><br>But I'm getting way ahead of myself there. It's probably the disorientation talking because I'm still reeling from the <b>WHAT THE HELL HAPPENED???</b> pinging inside my brain. This review will probably echo a lot of 2-star sentiments but I ended up giving it a hopeful 3 because something about Connor still reminds me a little of Jack Bauer.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388766328ra/7924384.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>The biggest chunk of the story concerns Lev and Connor on their way back to Ohio, to uncover the mystery behind the Rheinschilds and their old, severed ties with the Proactive Citizenry (PC). But the road to Akron is paved with wayward ostriches, small-town idiots and, unbeknownst to either, vengeful former Juvey cops. A few of these end up hampering our two heroes with health issues (of course) and <s>Raymond Babbitt</s> Grace Skinner, a low-cortical strategy savant. This forces them to make a pit-stop to the Arapache Reservation to seek ironic asylum since Lev pretty much left the place burdened with guilt and pain back in Unstrung.<br><br>Risa has escaped the clutches of Roberta's public relations machine and eventually finds sanctuary in a revival commune with a person from Lev's past. While Cam continues to be the poster boy for PC's Rewinding campaign while secretly hatching plans to destroy the organization in the name of Risa's love. <br><br>The members of the Stork Club who survived the plane crash are now being led by Starkey and Bam as a full-fledged terror group wreaking havoc and liberating unwinds from harvest clinics.<br><br>Now put all of those together in a box, shake well and throw them in the air. Who ever lands closest to each other will eventually find their way to that group's quest/mission/personal space in five chapters or more. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Connor realizes that everything has now changed, and their lives have become infinitely complicated.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388766328ra/7924385.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't know if that was a joke, considering how apt and how often this applies to every plot progression this series ever dished out. But there's a limit to how much I'd enjoy these kinds of twists. Too often it just becomes a pointless whim (what's the point of the Nelson chapters again?). To be blunt, Risa and CyFi's encounter felt bizarre and senseless. Does Risa really need to meet CyFi to "galvanize her belief to end unwinding once and for all"? Risa, the girl who opted to be a paraplegic than get a new, unwound spine? That Risa? <br><br>Speaking of, Risa's easily one of the strongest heroines I've read in a while and I really liked how she ended in <i>Unwind</i>. In <i>Unwholly</i> she gets a new pair of legs. Here, she gets a makeover, because she's on the run and needs a disguise. But I'm starting to feel I've lost the Risa I've loved from <i>Unwind</i> as she gets reconstructed to *that* kind of heroine. You know, the one in the middle of a love triangle? The way she was written in the Akron scenes was just like jumping from a cliff and taking ten paces back from where her character has evolved so far. I had high hopes that Shusterman, with all the existential conflict he so smartly presents, would handle the Connor-Risa-Cam story line with better treatment but with how things ended here, I am very nervous. <br><br>Speaking of conflicts, this somehow left me feeling hollow after finishing it. I do realize that the pit stops Lev, Connor and Risa encountered here somehow functions as a last temptation of sorts. Seducing them from their quests, making them second guess their capabilities to exact any change. But the execution leaves a lot to be desired. Once I finished <i>Unwind</i> and <i>Unwholly</i> I found myself questioning existence, the concept of the soul and the ethics behind the prospect of unwinding should it be a scientific reality. Once I finished Unsouled I am left with an unresolved love triangle, an unrecognizable Lev and the promise of Una and the Arapache's bigger roles in the next book. <br><br>I could hardly recognize <i>Unsouled</i> as part of this dystology were it not for Hayden, Bam and Starkey's story line and Connor's dynamic with "Roland" (the "Spank the monkey with your own damn hand" was just golden). I liked Grace as a new character, I just wish she wasn't stuck with the company she was with in the majority of this book.<br><br>The narrative was clunked down by the endless recapping and the humor fell flat more often than not. The shaky logic that I was willing to let pass in the first two books were piled on with more questionable developments. It's almost as if this book is hell bent on <b>REVERSE CONVINCING</b> me that it makes sense. Cam's charm just brushes with arrogance and douchiness a little too often and I can't even start with Lev without wanting to hurt something fluffy.<br><br>For something that started with such a radical premise, this somehow devolved into a stereotypical young adult romance with excessive padding of unnecessary characters and the bizarre need for everyone in this story to know everyone else. Is there going to be a tea party at the end and these are pre-emptive measures so no one gets awkward? <br><br>I would still pick up the last (please tell me its the last) book of this series out of my faith in this author's ability to squeeze my guts painfully and rattle my brain with unanswerable questions. Don't sink to tired tropes, dad jokes and YA-romance stereotypes, Neal Shusterman. You are not the GAP.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388766328ra/7924386.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://ashwednesday.booklikes.com/post/748276/be-better-than-the-gap" rel="nofollow noopener">Also on BookLikes.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="742684348553882073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1155745465" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1155745465" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15976696-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416179408p2/15976696.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1155745465?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/15976696-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19432805-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=awww">awww</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=broken-boys">broken-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=exhausting-reads">exhausting-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=love-the-characters">love-the-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=mindfuckery">mindfuckery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15976696-rose?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1155745465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5868755839559599945">This review contains spoilers for <i>UnSouled</i>. You've been warned.<br/><br/><i>UnSouled</i> was a bit disappointing, if I'm honest. I was pretty annoyed with having to read SO MUCH from POVs I couldn't care less about (e.g. Nelson, Argent, Cam, Starkey), it felt at times like I was reading more from POVs I couldn't give a fuck about than from the characters I actually cared about and who are actually the main characters of the series. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Risa was missing quite a lot, sure, she was there but it felt like</span></span>
  <span id="freeText5868755839559599945" style="display:none">This review contains spoilers for <i>UnSouled</i>. You've been warned.<br /><br /><i>UnSouled</i> was a bit disappointing, if I'm honest. I was pretty annoyed with having to read SO MUCH from POVs I couldn't care less about (e.g. Nelson, Argent, Cam, Starkey), it felt at times like I was reading more from POVs I couldn't give a fuck about than from the characters I actually cared about and who are actually the main characters of the series. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Risa was missing quite a lot, sure, she was there but it felt like I barely read from her POV. Also, her being gone from the "group" (Lev, Connor) for most part of the book made it quite boring at times to read her and/or Lev's/Connor's POVs. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, a thing that bugged me to NO END: Everyone losing each other. As in, not losing each other as in someone dying and not being there anymore but more like everyone forever getting into situations where they're losing each other and thus spending so much time apart from each other. And this made the book such a drag to read at times for me, I think. I love it when the trio is together (Risa, Connor, Lev) and the addition of Grace would make for a fun dynamic, if only EVERYONE WOULD BE TOGETHER AND STAY TOGETHER FOR ONCE. Seriously, I can't stress enough how annoying it was for me to read from POVs I honestly couldn't care less about AND THEN having to deal with EVERYONE always losing each other and thus reading about everyone being alone at some point or other (sometimes for a short time, other times FOR ALMOST THE WHOLE BOOK <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(talking about Risa here, obviously) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), which was just really boring at times and not only that, but also made it a pretty exhausting reading experience because getting to good parts took quite a while if you have to struggle through reading stuff you just didn't feel like reading.<br /><br />I get it, they're AWOL Unwinds and on the run and losing each other is nothing that I'd say is unrealistic, it's just that when these characters are apart, it easily gets boring to read about them all being on their own. While reading book one and book two, I couldn't flip the pages fast enough but while reading book three, whenever a new chapter about someone I couldn't care less about was up next, even if I felt like reading, I put my Kindle aside because I really didn't feel like reading from that person's POV. And while Shusterman managed in the previous installments to even make me look forward to reading from POVs of characters I didn't care much about, here it just wasn't the case.<br /><br />Apart from that, another thing that bugged me quite a lot: the reunion scene. Can we just get this straight, I waited almost THE WHOLE BOOK for everyone to get together again (for the reunion between Risa and Connor especially) and then it ends up being a totally awkward cringe-fest that didn't satisfy me like I hoped it would AT ALL. First of all, Cam was there and I thought that wouldn't be a problem but Risa made it one by just doing... nothing, basically. No jumping into each other's arms, nope, that just wasn't happening, no TALK ABOUT STUFF THAT WENT ON WHILE THEY'VE BEEN APART, nope, that just wasn't happening, instead it turned into a love-triangle-ish awkwardness between Risa, Cam and Connor and I was like, WHY PERQUE WIESO is this happening, while THERE IS MORE IMPORTANT STUFF GOING ON and THIS SHOULD NOT BE THE TIME TO INTRODUCE A LOVE TRIANGLE!!!11!1!! I was kind of done with the book by then, to be honest.<br /><br />But no matter what, I enjoyed it, which might be hard to believe seeing all the stuff I complained about but it's true. These characters have grown on me and even if I was a bit disappointed with how this sequel turned out to be, I still enjoyed spending time with the characters. I just hope that the fourth book will have less of boring/annoying POVs and more POVs from people I care about and that the love triangle mess will resolved as soon as possible and THAT ALL THESE KIDS JUST STAY TOGETHER FOR ONCE, DAMN IT.<br /><br />Overall, <i>UnSouled</i> is so far the weakest installment in the series that I had to struggle through a little but I still can't wait to read the fourth book and see how the series concludes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5868755839559599945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_736197649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/736197649" />
    <a title="Jenn (One of Many, We are Legion)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion"><img alt="Jenn (One of Many, We are Legion)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408317710p2/3003455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/736197649?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn (One of Many, We are Legion)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn (One of Many, We are Legion)" href="/user/show/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion">Jenn (One of Many, We are Legion)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781442423718" href="/book/show/17334101-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=psychologically-wrought-characters">psychologically-wrought-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=other">other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=young-adult-and-new-adult">young-adult-and-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=dystopia-and-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-and-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3003455-jenn-one-of-many-we-are-legion?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer736197649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4116292142473009251">I'm loving this thought-provoking series, so I can forgive some of the glaring editing issues (I noted a few typos towards the end). There were also a few moments when the book dragged a little bit, but for the most part it kept up the pace. That said, I was really surprised to get to the end and find out this was not the conclusion of the series. Thank god, because there are so many loose ends to wrap up still.<br/><br/>The political elements of this series have diverged far from where it began. At the o</span>
  <span id="freeText4116292142473009251" style="display:none">I'm loving this thought-provoking series, so I can forgive some of the glaring editing issues (I noted a few typos towards the end). There were also a few moments when the book dragged a little bit, but for the most part it kept up the pace. That said, I was really surprised to get to the end and find out this was not the conclusion of the series. Thank god, because there are so many loose ends to wrap up still.<br /><br />The political elements of this series have diverged far from where it began. At the outset, it seemed that a war between pro-choice and pro-life factions led to the Unwind accords. Not so. Shusterman has far more to say than that. There are a ton of layers going on here that are directly applicable to current US politics, corporate growth, and advertising. Shusterman has a very sinister and cynical outlook. In a nutshell, humans, mainly those without power, are entirely disposable and exist solely to benefit those at the top of the pyramid. In a typical sci-fi fashion, the book almost serves as a warning for the dangers of technology, particularly biotech.<br /><br />Basically, a mega-corporation buys the patents and tech for unwinding. A watchdog group (think SuperPAC) set up to oversee the ethical use of this tech becomes turncoat at some point and basically becomes a lobbyist for mega corp. It takes out ads supporting and opposing various laws so that no matter what, mega corp wins. It plays both sides. As Shusterman points out through a flashback: <i>"If he tries to rattle his saber at Proactive Citizenry, what good will it do? They haven't actually broken the law. They never do! Instead they mold the law to encompass whatever it is they wish to accomplish."</i><br /><br />Of course, it's way more complex than that and I don't mean to oversimplify his words. I still laud him for writing about issues like this for a book intended to be read by teens. They should be thinking about the greater picture, especially as they reach voting age.<br /><br />Oh, Starkey, how I hate you. Get the hell over your abandonment issues and stop projecting your shit onto everyone else acting like you're so noble for "freeing" people when, in actuality, you're just on some mission of vengeance because you were storked. You pretend like you're a savior for unwinds, but if there were no storks those camps, you would not be there. Get over yourself, asshole. He's such a damn hypocrite, too, with the cold blooded killing. He has serious mommy issues. It's a credit to Shusterman's character building skills that I hate Starkey so damn much.<br /><br />A weird thought I had. The unwound "parts" seem to have sense memory and the recipients usually take on some of the traits of the former person. Moreover, being unwound is not death in this world. Is this immortality? Are the individual parts still aware even when not connected to anything?<br /><br />Anyway, the end. YES, THE END! I don't want to get into details about it, and I don't think I would call it a cliffhanger, but he definitely threw out some breadcrumbs (loaves of bread, really) for the future of this series. I am excited as hell to find out the who/what/why behind all the unwinding and what their ultimate goals are. The revelation(no spoilers) he threw down about unwinding and why it persists were a bit of a blindside. I also love Sonia's storyline (her story is so sad!) and I am very excited to see her get justice. She's playing a long game. Very calculated. I can't wait for the next one (it'll be a long wait, sadly, since this book is still new).</span>
  <a data-text-id="4116292142473009251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_742491734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742491734" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/742491734?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442423695" href="/book/show/17334446-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dumb-science">dumb-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=great-premise">great-premise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=evul-people-are-evul">evul-people-are-evul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=evul-scientists">evul-scientists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=shitty-parents">shitty-parents</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=daddy-issues-mummy-issues">daddy-issues-mummy-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=emo-hero">emo-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=some-good-characters-some-bad">some-good-characters-some-bad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742491734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16271278919051858327"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>Not as gripping as the first book (<i>Unwind</i>) but still a decent enough read. The best thing about the series for me is the horrifying premise, where parents can decide to get their kids (from age 13 to 18) unwound (their bodies taken apart and organs harvested). Unfortunately, most of the other aspects of the dystopian world is pretty much the same as other YA dystopias. For example: the primary antagonist is the US government, the teenage protagonists are on the run/in hiding and being ch</span>
  <span id="freeText16271278919051858327" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />Not as gripping as the first book (<i>Unwind</i>) but still a decent enough read. The best thing about the series for me is the horrifying premise, where parents can decide to get their kids (from age 13 to 18) unwound (their bodies taken apart and organs harvested). Unfortunately, most of the other aspects of the dystopian world is pretty much the same as other YA dystopias. For example: the primary antagonist is the US government, the teenage protagonists are on the run/in hiding and being chased by various bad guys, there's a teeny bopper romance or two, most of the adults are evul bastards, there's nowhere to turn to apart from the odd adult, there's a huge conspiracy or two, a random power hungry character, the teens have to somehow overthrow the bad guys etc, etc. Yea, it's all been done before.<br /> <br /><b>Random thoughts:</b><br /><br />-Most of the story threads seemed to go nowhere for the majority of the book. In book 1, Connor/Risa/Lev were on the run and hiding from various bad guys (Proactive Citizenry/juvie cops/parts pirate), and they were doing the exact same thing in this one. Where's the story progression? Sure, they'd each gone through different experiences: Connor escaping Unwinding and gaining infamy, Risa being used by Proactive Citizenry, and Lev changing from a naive willing tithe to a bitter-jaded-experienced teenager… But that was more character progression, they were essentially doing the same bloody thing as when they first escaped being unwound. It was only at the end when things started to change, and they got some power and knowledge that could help them in their fight against unwinding… I was just annoyed I had to read hundreds of pages of the characters just running, hiding, and fighting — it got quite boring.<br /><br />-The characters were a bit of a mixed bag. I wasn't impressed with Connor, Lev, Risa, or Nelson. I found Connor and Lev rather boring, Risa was judgmental and annoying, and Nelson was one dimensional. Nelson's whole arc was rubbish, his obsession with hunting Connor and Lev so he could sell them to parts pirates was really dull. I'm not a fan of bad guys who are bad guys just because the protagonist humiliated/bested them and they can't get over it and thus are hellbent on revenge. It all's so unoriginal and cliched<br /><br />-The POV's I enjoyed most were Starkey and Cam's. They took action, and tried to change things for themselves and other people. Unlike the other main characters that just hid and ran to various different places and people. <br /><br />-I was so glad that Cam turned against Roberta (his maker), she was a fucked up cow. And Starkey's arc was entertaining because it was so obvious that his arrogance and recklessness would eventually get him killed, I'm looking forward to him crashing and burning in the final book.<br /><br />-I really hope that the letters Sonia has kept will be brought up in the next book, I'd love to see the reaction from all those parents when they receive a letter from their possibly dead child who they agreed to have unwound. <br /><br />-I really liked Hayden and Bam teaming up, I'm hoping they take down Starkey.<br /><br />-There were way too many POV's, unless the book is really long then I prefer no more than three POV characters.<br /><br />-I wasn't a fan of the present tense narration, probably because I'm so used to reading books written in past tense. <br /><br />All in all, an enjoyable read… It would have been more interesting though if there'd been more going on in certain character arcs, because a lot of it felt rather uninspired and repetitive. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16271278919051858327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1780039420" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1780039420" />
    <a title="Paula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9829355-paula"><img alt="Paula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362921990p2/9829355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1780039420?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula" href="/user/show/9829355-paula">Paula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/28808225-unsouled">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=heart-wrenching">heart-wrenching</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=captivating">captivating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=amazon">amazon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=ya-angst-coming-of-age">ya-angst-coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=series-i-m-reading">series-i-m-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9829355-paula?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1780039420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8100801898872960556">There is just no letting up. Neal Shusterman doesn't let the reader catch a breath. Everytime I'm foolish enough to think that things are getting better and all will be good, he just destroys me all over again. And because I'm a glutton for punishment, I still can't stop reading. <br/>What those kids have to go through, what they have to endure - it's beyond the imaginable. And yet, somehow it is so fitting to the current situation in the world. It's like commentary on what is happening these days. I</span>
  <span id="freeText8100801898872960556" style="display:none">There is just no letting up. Neal Shusterman doesn't let the reader catch a breath. Everytime I'm foolish enough to think that things are getting better and all will be good, he just destroys me all over again. And because I'm a glutton for punishment, I still can't stop reading. <br />What those kids have to go through, what they have to endure - it's beyond the imaginable. And yet, somehow it is so fitting to the current situation in the world. It's like commentary on what is happening these days. It's frightening in a way how poignant Neal Shusterman is with his observations, with his assessment of people and society. I'm baffled. <br /><br />The story is keeping me on my toes. It's making me breathless. There is suspense and action. But there is also so much pain and heartache. And in between all that destruction and despair, you still find kindness, beauty and love. Few and far in between, but it's there. And it helps to stomach the sadness of the story. To not get lost in the darkness. <br /><br />I love so many of the characters. And ones that I hated at the beginning, I came to love now. But my favorites in this book are definitely Connor, Hayden and Grace. Especially Grace, because while everyone thing she's a fry short of a happy meal, she's smarter and kinder and stronger than anyone gives her credit for. And I have the feeling she'll be the one to help save the day. <br /><br />5 this-is-addictive stars. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8100801898872960556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gIiN7G5fo3ebFHwnNWnmjLY1BYw3yqZidhezBxkglOM36QdqTdOCF69eR4tOinnwDOfyXZHYe3cAeIuUqGGphw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CtsNFwOxgCa61G8CBUB33+BlYyv9abvITBQE31C3EQe9uoeRID2hRo6eVK5+o+ijWreU+lt7Zt06ezxM4fYsYw==')})
  }

          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/19564.Neal_Shusterman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1246977170p3/19564.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/19564.Neal_Shusterman">Neal Shusterman

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7622786069223307572">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movi</span>
  <span id="freeText7622786069223307572" style="display:none">Award-winning author Neal Shusterman grew up in Brooklyn, New York, where he began writing at an early age. After spending his junior and senior years of high school at the American School of Mexico City, Neal went on to UC Irvine, where he made his mark on the UCI swim team, and wrote a successful humor column. Within a year of graduating, he had his first book deal, and was hired to write a movie script.<br /><br />In the years since, Neal has made his mark as a successful novelist, screenwriter, and television writer. As a full-time writer, he claims to be his own hardest task-master, always at work creating new stories to tell. His books have received many awards from organizations such as the International Reading Association, and the American Library Association, as well as garnering a myriad of state and local awards across the country. Neal's talents range from film directing (two short films he directed won him the coveted CINE Golden Eagle Awards) to writing music and stage plays – including book and lyrical contributions to “American Twistory,” which is currently playing in Boston. He has even tried his hand at creating Games, having developed three successful "How to Host a Mystery" game for teens, as well as seven "How to Host a Murder" games.<br /><br />As a screen and TV writer, Neal has written for the "Goosebumps" and “Animorphs” TV series, and wrote the Disney Channel Original Movie “Pixel Perfect”. Currently Neal is adapting his novel Everlost as a feature film for Universal Studios.<br /><br />Wherever Neal goes, he quickly earns a reputation as a storyteller and dynamic speaker. Much of his fiction is traceable back to stories he tells to large audiences of children and teenagers -- such as his novel The Eyes of Kid Midas. As a speaker, Neal is in constant demand at schools and conferences. Degrees in both psychology and drama give Neal a unique approach to writing. Neal's novels always deal with topics that appeal to adults as well as teens, weaving true-to-life characters into sensitive and riveting issues, and binding it all together with a unique and entertaining sense of humor.<br /><br />Of Everlost, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman has reimagined what happens after death and questions power and the meaning of charity. While all this is going on, he has also managed to write a rip-roaring adventure…”<br /><br />Of What Daddy Did, Voice of Youth Advocates wrote; "This is a compelling, spell-binding story... A stunning novel, impossible to put down once begun.<br /><br />Of The Schwa Was Here, School Library Journal wrote: “Shusterman's characters–reminiscent of those crafted by E. L. Konigsburg and Jerry Spinelli–are infused with the kind of controlled, precocious improbability that magically vivifies the finest children's classics.<br /><br />Of Scorpion Shards, Publisher's Weekly wrote: "Shusterman takes an outlandish comic-book concept, and, through the sheer audacity and breadth of his imagination makes it stunningly believable. A spellbinder."<br /><br />And of The Eyes of Kid Midas, The Midwest Book Review wrote "This wins our vote as one of the best young-adult titles of the year" and was called "Inspired and hypnotically readable" by School Library Journal.<br /><br />Neal Shusterman lives in Southern California with his children Brendan, Jarrod, Joelle, and Erin, who are a constant source of inspiration!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7622786069223307572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Ridding society of troublesome teens while simltaneously providing much-needed tissues for transplant might be convenient, but its morality has finally been brought into question. However, unwinding has become big business, and there are powerful political and corporate interests that want to see it not only continue, but also expand to the unwinding of prisoners and the impoverished.\n\nCam is a product of unwinding; made entirely out of the parts of other unwinds, he is a teen who does not technically exist.
